Mystery Surrounding Seaman He Baosheng's Death: Union to Negotiate Strictly with Company 106

The Preparatory Committee of the China Seamen's Union has recently received a report from the family of He Baosheng, a Chinese seaman on the 英商 老太古 Company's 萊克西拿 ship, regarding the discovery of his body on the ocean surface. It will begin active negotiations to secure generous compensation for the family of the deceased in order to fulfill its responsibility to protect them. At the same time, it is actively investigating the truth of He Baosheng's death in order to obtain the facts before proceeding. He Baosheng was a coppersmith on the 萊克西拿 ship. His body was found on the ocean surface near Nafu in the United States on June 11th of last year. The causes of death were rumored to be various. Some said that he was murdered and his body was thrown into the sea to cover up the crime. Others said that he was addicted to gambling and committed suicide due to debt. Therefore, the truth remains to be investigated. The rumors are not credible. The 萊克西拿 ship arrived in Shanghai once on May 18th of this year. Prior to that, the Shanghai Public Security Bureau had received an order to investigate, and the Secretariat of the Municipal Government had sent a letter to the union for assistance. When the ship arrived, the detective team sent personnel to meet with the Seamen's Union to wait at the dock. They boarded the ship and called out the seamen from the engine room and stokehold to inquire. There were no suspicious points. The detective team members then took four people to the team: the stokehold foreman Tu Decai, the seaman foreman Jiang Fucai, the stoker Chen Yuebei, and the seaman Le A'er. Those arrested, including Tu Decai, were purely good people. Since being arrested, the seafarer groups in this city have risen up to rescue them. Furthermore, because the 萊克西拿 ship was about to sail, they could not stay ashore for long, resulting in their dismissal by the company. Subsequently, the Yan Ying General Agency and other seafarer groups jointly petitioned the union to provide bail. For the sake of caution, the union first sent personnel to ask the detective team about the reasons for the detention. It was learned that it was for the purpose of inquiry, not arrest. It then moved them to the union for questioning. However, after strict questioning, they did not know anything about He Baosheng's death and could not be suspected. It was also found that the ship was indeed scheduled to sail the next day (21st). In order to avoid innocent people being implicated, it agreed to the request of the seafarer groups and allowed the four people, Tu Decai, to be released on bail and return to the ship to await investigation. They were released on bail and returned to the ship on the 10th of last month. The guarantors were the Yan Ying General Agency and other five seafarer groups in this city, as well as the Shanghai National Trade Company. They all signed a guarantee and deposited it with the union, assuming all responsibility for Tu Decai, etc. Since the family of the deceased has petitioned the union to handle the matter, it will not be difficult to find out the truth after the union investigates He Baosheng's murder or suicide, and the issue of compensation for the family of the deceased will certainly have a satisfactory result.

Page 10

French Gift of Books to the Oriental Library; Presentation Ceremony Held Yesterday 107

More than Two Hundred Chinese and Foreign Dignitaries Attended; French Consul-General Presented Books; Chu Minyi and Others Delivered Speeches; Over a Thousand Volumes to be Exhibited Today and Tomorrow

The French Philanthropic Society's donation of 1,600 French books to the Oriental Library was celebrated yesterday afternoon at 5:30 PM with a presentation ceremony held in the grand auditorium of the French Municipal Council, located at 11 Avenue des Soeurs. Details are as follows:

Attending Guests

Attendees at yesterday's ceremony included Chu Minyi, representing Wang Jingwei, President of the Executive Yuan of the National Government; Hong Kui, representing Wu Tiecheng, Mayor of Shanghai; Cai Yuanpei; Li Shizeng; Paul Pelliot; Wang Jingqi; Wu Guangjian; Ding Rong; Hu Dunfu; Wang Simao; Xu Shiying; Zhou Ren; Zhao Housheng; Yang Weiyu; Li Quanshi; Chen Hexian; Wang Boqi; Lu Gaoyi; Qi Yunqing; Zhang Yuanruo; He Dekui; Xu Xinliu; Chen Zhuzun, and others, as well as representatives from academic organizations stationed in Shanghai from various countries, members of the Philanthropic Society, members of the Oriental Library Revitalization Committee, and journalists from Chinese and foreign newspapers and news agencies, totaling over three hundred people. The auditorium was adorned with both Chinese and French flags, serving as a profound symbol of the friendship and academic exchange between the two nations. The presentation ceremony was solemn and grand.

Speech by the French Consul

The Consul-General could not attend today due to other engagements and expresses his deep regret. I am honored to be present on his behalf and to present these books from the French Concession Philanthropic Society to the Oriental Library. I believe that this will further advance the cultural exchange between China and France, and further strengthen the friendship between our two countries. French citizens deeply admire the Commercial Press's rapid recovery and its efforts in revitalizing the Oriental Library. This book donation is merely a small gesture of our support.

Speech by Paul Pelliot

Mr. Pelliot gave a lengthy speech, briefly stating that the dignitaries present at today's grand event, besides the members of the Oriental Library Revitalization Committee, Chairman Zhang Yuanji, Standing Committee members Wang Yunwu and Cai Yuanpei, also include Mr. Chu Minyi and Mr. Li Shizeng. Mr. Cai, Mr. Chu, and Mr. Li are all powerful figures dedicated to promoting cultural exchange between China and the West. In particular, they have established many initiatives in Sino-French cultural cooperation. Mr. Li Shizeng is the founder of the Sino-French Cultural Association. Mr. Zhang Yuanji is a renowned Chinese scholar with deep ties to the Commercial Press. He has been able to apply modern corporate organizational methods to lead the Commercial Press to its current glorious state. As for Mr. Wang Yunwu, he is also a scholar and inventor of a Chinese character indexing system, as well as a businessman. The Commercial Press's swift recovery after being destroyed is naturally attributable to Mr. Wang. I am deeply honored to be among so many scholars today, and especially proud to have participated in the selection of books for this donation. The books cover a wide range of subjects and are all fundamental classics, which will hopefully contribute to the exchange of academic knowledge between China and France. The Chinese nation has a long history and occupies an important position in world culture. It has been progressing rapidly in recent years and has a bright future. The French people have always been friends of China, and I extend my best wishes on behalf of the French.

Speech by Zhang Yuanji

Chairman of the Oriental Library Revitalization Committee, Zhang Yuanji, spoke as follows: Mr. Consul-General Bodes and esteemed guests, today, the Oriental Library is receiving a donation of over a thousand rare books from the French Philanthropic Society, and we have the honor of hearing remarks from Mr. Bodes, the French Consul-General in Shanghai, representing the Society. As Chairman of the Oriental Library Revitalization Committee, I accept this gift on behalf of the Library and offer my sincere gratitude. We all know that while Sino-Western cultural exchange began quite early, it became more systematic in the 17th century. Although scholars from various countries have served as intermediaries in this exchange, we can confidently say that the most credit is due to the scholars of the French Jesuit Order and modern French Sinologists. These French scholars not only brought Western science and Christianity to China, but also introduced Chinese political philosophy, ethics, agricultural technology, and art to Europe. As a result, European thought and art in the 18th century were influenced by Chinese culture. French Rococo artists such as Watteau and political thinkers of the Encyclopedia school, as well as economic thinkers of the Quesnay school, were all products of Sino-Western cultural fusion. Many modern French scholars have a deep understanding of Chinese culture, most notably Mr. Chavannes and Mr. Pelliot, who are especially worthy of our respect. More than a decade ago, I had the opportunity to visit Mr. Chavannes during my travels in Europe and had a delightful conversation. Today, Mr. Pelliot is here to give us a valuable lecture, which is a great honor. Therefore, it is the French who have made the most efforts to promote Sino-Western cultural exchange, and it is also the French who have contributed the most to making Sino-Western culture mutually influential. Today, the French Philanthropic Society's donation of books to the Oriental Library is a strong indication of the French people's continued efforts to promote Sino-Western cultural exchange. I believe that not only the Oriental Library Revitalization Committee should be grateful to our French friends, but we Chinese people should also be grateful to modern French scholars for their efforts to promote Chinese culture. To express our gratitude, we are presenting a copy of the rare edition of the Siku Quanshu recently published by the Commercial Press as a token of our continued Sino-French cultural exchange. On behalf of the Oriental Library Revitalization Committee, I would like to thank the French Philanthropic Society for its generous donation of valuable books, Mr. Li Rong, the French member of the Oriental Library Revitalization Committee, for his tireless efforts for the Oriental Library over the years, which made this donation possible, and Mr. Bodes, the Consul-General, for presiding over today's presentation ceremony. At the same time, I would also like to thank all the distinguished guests.

Speech by President Wang

Secretary-General Chu Minyi delivered a speech on behalf of President Wang of the Executive Yuan. Although our Oriental Library is a private institution, its collection of books is the most complete and comprehensive. Among the public and private libraries in the southeastern provinces of our country, none can compare to it. Its destruction in the war was a great loss to our nation's culture. Now, the Library is re-collecting books, and although it cannot immediately restore its former glory, it is still a treasure trove of books in Shanghai, thanks to the support of various parties. Recently, the French Philanthropic Society donated over a thousand books and held a presentation ceremony this month, along with a public exhibition. I am here on behalf of the President of the Executive Yuan to attend and receive the generous intentions of our friendly country, which only increases my feelings. I recall that during the European War, a large library in Leuven, Belgium, was destroyed by fire, but after it was restored, countries from all over the world competed to donate books, and within a few years, it once again became a grand sight. This is because culture is a tool for advancing humanity, and books are the embodiment of culture. All civilized nations value this, and therefore, they are willing to support such endeavors. Today, our Oriental Library accepts the generosity of our friendly country, gaining countless works by specialized scholars from civilized nations. We know that other friendly nations will surely share the same sentiments and continue to offer their support. This is what we can confidently expect, based on the past example of the Leuven Library. Therefore, while expressing my gratitude to the French Philanthropic Society, I also offer these thoughts.

Speeches by Wu and Li

Secretary Hong delivered a speech on behalf of Mayor Wu, briefly stating that Mayor Wu could not attend in person due to other engagements and that he was representing him. Before its destruction, the Oriental Library was a rich asset of China. After its destruction, thanks to the efforts of the Revitalization Committee, the Oriental Library has now received a donation of valuable books from the French Philanthropic Society, selected by the Sinologist Mr. Pelliot. This not only enriches the Sino-Western culture but also reflects a deep friendship. I respectfully thank our friendly country on behalf of the Mayor and express my admiration for the efforts of the Oriental Library Revitalization Committee. Li Shizeng delivered a speech, briefly stating that he had just arrived in Shanghai from Beijing and was asked to attend on short notice, which made him reflect on some things. There are two kinds of spirits in humanity, one is unfortunate struggle, and the other is mutual assistance and cooperation. Today's gathering is a complete expression of mutual assistance and cooperation, and not just a local expression, but a large-scale performance of humanity as a whole. The unfortunate struggles of humanity will surely be changed by the development of the spirit of mutual assistance and cooperation. Today's meeting is an expression of cultural mutual assistance and cultural cooperation between China and France. This expression is very promising. The Oriental Library suffered greatly, but today's mutual assistance outweighs the sacrifice.

Revitalization Progress

Wang Yunwu reported on the revitalization progress of the Oriental Library as follows: Mr. Consul-General Bodes and esteemed guests, many of you present today have directly or indirectly supported the revitalization of the Oriental Library, and you certainly want to know about the past, present, and future of the Oriental Library. I, as the former director of the Oriental Library and current standing committee member of the Oriental Library Revitalization Committee, will give a brief report on these facts and expectations. The Oriental Library of the past, that is, the Oriental Library that was destroyed in the January 28 Incident, was founded thirty years ago by Mr. Zhang Yuanji when he was in charge of the Compilation and Translation Department of the Commercial Press. It was originally named Hanfenlou, and its initial collection focused on Chinese classical books and manuscripts, as well as rare books. More than a decade ago, I succeeded Mr. Zhang in his position, and I also actively collected foreign language books. In 1926, the Board of Directors of the Commercial Press decided to reorganize it into the Oriental Library, making its collection of Chinese and foreign language books available to the reading public. Since its opening, the operating expenses and the cost of acquiring new books have been approximately 60,000 to 70,000 yuan per year, all of which were borne by the Commercial Press. Before the January 28 Incident in 1932, the Library had a collection of 500,000 volumes of Chinese and foreign language books, of which about 80,000 volumes were in foreign languages, including over 10,000 volumes in French. In addition to rare Chinese books, there were also many rare foreign language books and complete sets of academic journals. The complete destruction of such a valuable collection was truly a great loss to culture, which is why people at home and abroad are optimistic about its revitalization. The Oriental Library of the present is the result of the establishment of the Oriental Library Revitalization Committee and the current situation. Based on its spirit of founding and maintaining the Oriental Library for the past thirty years, the Commercial Press decided within a year of the disaster, in the spring of 1933, that if there were any profits each year, one-third of the public welfare fund allocated according to regulations would be used exclusively for revitalizing the Oriental Library. In the first year, over 40,000 yuan was obtained, in the second year over 50,000 yuan, and in the third year over 70,000 yuan. In addition, Mr. Zhang Yuanji personally donated 10,000 yuan. Currently, the Oriental Library has a revitalization fund of approximately 190,000 yuan, and the Commercial Press allocates a new fund of 70,000 to 80,000 yuan each year, or at least 40,000 to 50,000 yuan. As for books, the Commercial Press has separately allocated funds to purchase reference books for its compilation and translation departments, following the method used before the Oriental Library was established. To date, over 120,000 volumes of Chinese and foreign books have been purchased, especially a large number of Chinese collectanea from various dynasties. These books will all be available for use by the Oriental Library in the future. Because of this rich collection of books, we can further engage in outreach. Recently, the Commercial Press compiled and printed a large-scale collectanea series for libraries and bibliophiles at home and abroad. This is tantamount to making the collection of a library available to libraries across the country, and even the world. On the other hand, thanks to the efforts of the Oriental Library Revitalization Committee and support committees at home and abroad, and the enthusiasm of Chinese and foreign scholars, approximately 20,000 volumes of Chinese and foreign language books have been received as donations. Now, with the enthusiastic support of the Shanghai French Concession Philanthropic Society, over a thousand kinds of valuable French books have been purchased and donated, for which we are extremely grateful. Regarding this generous donation, in addition to thanking the Shanghai French Concession Philanthropic Society, we must also credit Mr. Li Rong, the French member of the Oriental Library Revitalization Committee. At the same time, we are also extremely grateful to Professor Paul Pelliot for selecting the books for this donation, and to Mr. Bodes, the French Consul-General in Shanghai, and the French Municipal Council for supporting this charitable act. In the future, the Oriental Library will have an increasing number of books from donations and purchases made with funds allocated by the Commercial Press, and the increase will be very rapid. On the other hand, with an existing fund of nearly 200,000 yuan and new revenue of tens of thousands of yuan each year, it may not be difficult to have a more magnificent Oriental Library in Shanghai in the near future. However, to realize this hope, in addition to the continued efforts of the Oriental Library Revitalization Committee and the Commercial Press, we also need the support of all of you present today and enthusiastic people at home and abroad. The Shanghai French Concession Philanthropic Society's donation of a large number of valuable books to the Oriental Library has a great impact on the realization of this hope, and we will never forget it.

Public Exhibition

The books donated by France and the rare edition of the Siku Quanshu presented by the Commercial Press are on display on the second floor. They will be open to the public today and tomorrow. The book catalog includes: (1) Dictionaries, (2) French Literature, (3) Works by Famous French Figures, (4) Modern Poetry, (5) Modern Drama, (6) Modern Prose, (7) Philosophy and Sociology, (8) Experimental Education, (9) Science, (10) Art, (11) Architecture, (12) History, (13) Geography, (14) French Colonies, (15) Law, (16) Hygiene, (17) Sports, (18) Dissertations by Chinese Students Graduating from France.

China Merchants Steam Navigation Company to Take Over Inland River Steamers on Schedule; Zhejiang Construction Department Sends Commissioner to Handle Transfer 108

The board of directors of the state-run China Merchants Steam Navigation Company (China Merchants) resolved to take back the inland river steamer operations and manage them itself. After organizing a reorganization committee to prepare for the takeover, it was decided that the takeover would take place on the 15th. In addition to stipulating five routes, the remaining routes would still be contracted out to merchants. The details are as follows:

Reorganization Committee Formed to Prepare for Takeover

General Manager Liu Hongsheng informed his subordinates that the board of directors had resolved to take back the inland river steamer operations and manage them itself. The board also approved the formation of a reorganization committee with Sheng Qunian and Cai Pengcheng to make preparations. Please investigate and delegate personnel accordingly, etc. The General Manager has approved the matter and instructed it to be handled accordingly. He has also appointed Sheng Qunian, Cai Pengcheng, Chen Weiqing, Director of the General Affairs Department, Xu Guangde, Director of the Accounting Department, He Molin, Director of the Business Department, Zhao Yuntai, Director of the Shipbuilding Department, and Inspector Wei Xuezhou as members of the reorganization committee, etc. This is to inform you.

Routes Other than the Five to be Leased Out to Merchants

China Merchants announced yesterday that the China Merchants Inland River Steamer Bureau, which has been leased to the Zhejiang Provincial Construction Department since 1930, will have its contract expire on the 15th of this month. The company has decided to take it back and manage it itself. Apart from the five routes of Zhenqing, Shenhu, Lingshen, Hangshen, and Suhang, those who wish to lease other routes should immediately submit their terms to the General Affairs Department of the company for negotiation.

Transfer and Takeover Scheduled for the 15th

The expiration date of the inland river steamer lease is June 15th. The Zhejiang Construction Department has appointed Zhu Yanping and others to arrive in Shanghai from Hangzhou yesterday to first contact Zhang Jinglun, the sub-lessee merchant, and then negotiate the transfer procedures with China Merchants. The reorganization committee of China Merchants to take over the inland river steamer operations will hold a meeting within days to appoint personnel. It has been decided that the committee will jointly take over the Inland River Steamer Bureau with the Zhejiang Construction Department on the 15th of this month. As for the reorganization plan after the takeover, it has already been decided.

Zhang Yuexin's Entire Family Commits Suicide by Jumping from Building; Suicide Note Released 109

No One Can Help in Time after being Harmed by Business Partners; Charitable Organization Plans to Provide High-Quality Coffin and Burial

A tragedy occurred at the six-story pavilion at the main entrance of the Great World amusement park, at the corner of Avenue Petain and Rue Montigny in the French Concession, where an entire family of six tourists (three men and three women), old and young, committed suicide by jumping from the building. Five people died instantly, and a young man in his twenties was sent to Renji Hospital, where he died en route. The French police were informed and dispatched detectives to investigate. The bodies of all sizes were transported to the Tongren Fuyuan Funeral Home for examination. A suicide note was found in the pocket of the deceased wearing a Western suit, awaiting a report to the court for inspection. This was reported in yesterday's newspaper. Yesterday morning, the French Police Department reported the matter to the Second Special District Court Procuratorate, which appointed Prosecutor Wang Ren, along with forensic doctor Jiang, recorder Peng Yu, and others, to inspect the bodies at noon. Among the six bodies, the old woman and the seven- or eight-year-old girl had their heads and skulls smashed, with blood flowing all over their faces. The others all had clear and handsome features and died from internal organ injuries sustained in the fall. After the examination, the officials ascended to the courtroom, where police detective Zhang Chunsheng reported the investigation and presented the suicide note. After reviewing the suicide note, the official ordered the examination of the six unidentified bodies, both male and female, large and small, who died from injuries sustained in the fall. The bodies were handed over to Tongren Fuyuan Funeral Home for temporary storage, pending identification. After the examination, the official handed over the deceased's suicide note to the detectives, instructing them to take a photograph of the suicide note and submit it to the court for inclusion in the case file. The suicide note is transcribed as follows: "Recalling that my grandfather was generous and charitable, valuing righteousness and lightly regarding wealth, he built dozens of miles of roads, over ten bridges, and rebuilt seven or eight temples, including the Sanyi Temple, Yue Wu Temple, and Confucius Temple. He provided firewood and rice to poor neighbors and friends. The amount of money owed to my family was no less than hundreds of thousands, but my grandfather and my late father did not seek repayment and burned the account books. This can be said to be a family that does good deeds. However, because of helping a friend in distress, we were harmed and lost 450,000吊. Then, we were harmed by an ungrateful and inhuman administrator, who secretly transferred and misappropriated our family's most prosperous business, causing it to collapse and lose 500,000 yuan. Alas, these are all past events, not worth mentioning. However, I think of my grandfather and my late father, who cherished orphans, cared for the elderly, and pitied the poor, performing countless secret acts of kindness and saving countless people. Now, my entire family of six, three generations of mothers, sons, and grandchildren, have suffered this tragic fate and thrown themselves into the fire. Who can help us in time? Although we value integrity and honor and regard death as a return home, we cannot help but resent heaven and worry about people. The so-called family that accumulates good deeds will surely have blessings to spare, and the laws of nature are clear, and retribution is cyclical, are truly empty words. Written by Zhang Yuexin." The letter was written on three sheets of white paper with blue grid lines of patriotic stationery. The writing is elegant, and the language is quite coherent, indicating that the writer had a considerable level of education. It is speculated that the deceased's family was originally wealthy but was harmed, leading to this extremely tragic suicide. However, the deceased's bodies were placed in the funeral home, and no one came to identify them until yesterday evening. According to an inspector at the amusement park, the deceased were seen playing in the amusement park for three days. The bound feet of the deceased old woman and middle-aged woman suggest that they were from the Hubei area. Mr. Guo Shaowen, the director of Tongren Fuyuan Funeral Home, considering the tragedy, could not bear to bury them in ordinary wooden coffins according to custom. He plans to wait until today and, if no one comes to identify them, will ask the directors of the funeral home to allocate high-quality clothing and coffins for burial and relocate them to the Pudong burial ground to await future identification by family members.

Competing for Hotel Guests Leads to Use of Knives 110

Chen Huaye is Severely Injured, Also Involves Debt Issues

Yu Qi, a Cantonese man working as a greeter at the New Asia Hotel on North Sichuan Road, had an argument with fellow Cantonese Chen Huaye near Wuchang Road and Chongming Road at 11:25 AM the previous day, due to competing for hotel guests. Chen was stabbed in the chest and lungs by Yu with a knife, causing serious injuries. Yu also suffered knife wounds to two fingers on his right hand. As a result, two Chinese constables No. 1667 and No. 1289, and Cantonese detective Feng Qi, arrived on the scene after hearing the alarm and took both Yu and Chen to the Hongkou Police Station, from where they were transferred to Tongren Hospital for treatment. Yu was taken into custody. Yesterday morning, he was brought before the Third Criminal Court of the First Special District Court. Lawyer Wang Yaotang of the Municipal Council stated that the case originated from a guest named Yu Jinhe who arrived in Shanghai from Guangdong and stayed temporarily in room 403 of the hotel. According to hotel custom, guests who come to Shanghai for the first time and are unfamiliar with the city must be accompanied by a greeter to various places. Chen had initially contacted the Yu guest, but the defendant subsequently went to the room and claimed that he knew the guest and should accompany him on the sightseeing trip, which led to a dispute and also involved debt issues. Chen stated at the police station that the defendant had been arrested for smoking opium at the Taoyuanli opium den on North Zhejiang Road and taken to court, where he was fined 30 yuan. Chen had paid the fine on his behalf, but the defendant had only repaid 12 yuan after being released, and the remaining amount had not been repaid to date. This morning, he had argued with the defendant once over the unpaid debt. It had nothing to do with guiding the guest. At that time, the defendant pushed him down and stabbed him with a knife, etc. He is currently seriously injured in the hospital and cannot attend the court. The defendant claimed that the victim used to run an opium den and owed him 20 yuan for opium. He had repaid two yuan. When he tried to collect the debt, the victim took out a knife and stabbed him. He seized the opportunity to resist and accidentally injured the victim in the chest, hence the injuries to his right fingers. However, the two Chinese constables did not witness the fight, and the knife was not recovered. Both sides have different versions of the story, and the situation is complicated. The case should be postponed so that the victim can recover from his injuries, etc. When questioned, the defendant's testimony was evasive. Judge Jiang Shuzi ordered him to be remanded in custody and the matter to be further investigated at a later date.

It is expected that there will be a grand occasion in the future. Space is limited, so participants should register as soon as possible to avoid missing out.

In Front of the Da Fang Hotel, Bandits Kidnap and Rob 112

Victim Released Mid-Journey, Total Loot Reaches Seven Thousand Yuan

The Hetai Money Exchange and Cigarette Paper Shop, located at No. 87 Zhonghua Lane, Zhengjia Muqiao Street, French Concession, is owned by Yu Heqing from Ningbo. He usually supplements his income by promoting new banknotes for various banks. Recently, because the shop used counterfeit “double dime” coins, the French police investigated and confiscated 1,391 counterfeit "jiao" coins. He was prosecuted in the Special Court No. 2, sentenced to three months in prison and fined 300 yuan. He is currently appealing on bail. Yesterday morning around 9:00 AM, Yu ordered his shop assistant, Le Jinzhang, to take 7,000 yuan in cash in his own chartered car to the China Industrial Bank on the Museum Road to exchange for the bank's banknotes. As Le's car, pulled by the driver Ah Fu (from Tongzhou), was heading north, passing Caishi Street and reaching the front of No. 30 opposite the Da Fang Hotel, suddenly two bandits jumped out of a car parked by the roadside, blocking Le's rickshaw. They forced Le out of the rickshaw. At the same time, two other bandits rushed up, dragged Le out of the rickshaw, and, together with the bag of banknotes, pushed him into the car parked by the roadside. The bandits knocked the rickshaw puller down and drove the car north, turning west onto Avenue Edward VII. Le's rickshaw puller, witnessing the scene, frantically shouted, "Robbery! Kidnapping!" Nearby detectives who heard the shouts arrived, but it was too late to chase them. The bandits grabbed the bag of banknotes from Le in the car. As the car traveled to West Dahua Road, Mu'er Ming Road, Jing'an Temple Road, the bandits stopped the car, hired a rickshaw, ordered Le to get out and ride in it slowly, and the kidnapping car sped off. The two bandits escorting Le fled not far after that. After being robbed, Le knew he was safe. He regained his composure, took a rickshaw back to the shop, informed the shop owner, and reported the robbery to the French police, requesting them to apprehend the robbers. The police telegraphed the Public Concession police and the Chinese Public Security Bureau to cooperate in the investigation. Subsequently, it was found that at 8:30 AM yesterday, two middle-aged men came to the Lihua Car Company at the Jiujiang Road and Zhejiang Road intersection, hiring a car to go to Fenglin Bridge in the Chinese district, paying a fare of two yuan. The cashier dispatched driver Cao Miaoqi (from Tongzhou) to drive car No. 18032 (French Concession) and No. 4437 (Chinese Concession). The two passengers then sat in the car. Cao drove to the Da Fang Hotel on Zhengjia Muqiao Road in the French Concession to wait for friends. Upon arriving in front of the Da Fang Hotel, the two passengers in the car greeted two men waiting by the roadside and spoke to them quietly, instructing the driver to wait. Unexpectedly, they were the robbers kidnapping the victim. Around 10:00 AM, the car was discovered at the Tokyo Road and Macau Road intersection, which is under the jurisdiction of the Putuo Road police station in the western suburbs of Shanghai. Patrol officers noticed it and reported it to the police station. Detectives were dispatched to investigate the car. The keys had been taken by the robbers. They tried to take the car back to the police station for verification. Meanwhile, the British and French police agencies dispatched detectives to investigate and apprehend the robbers.

Public Concession Police Department Intensively Investigates and Arrests Robbers 113

Twelve Robbers Arrested in Two Days, Large Number of Guns and Bullets Confiscated

Recently, due to the frequent occurrence of robbery cases in the Public Concession, the head of the Police Department ordered all police stations to intensify investigations and arrests. On the 4th and 5th of this month, the Huishi Police Station, as well as the Xinzha and Gordon Road police stations, successively arrested twelve robbers, confiscating five handguns, twenty-eight bullets, and one fake handgun. Details are recorded below: (1) Huishi Police Station Detective Chief Shang Wu and Detective Wang Youshan, acting on a tip-off, arrested Gu Wenming, Shen Xinbao, Tang Jinyuan, Shen Xiaolu, and Wang Agen at No. 14 Laozha Street, North Fujian Road, at 6:35 AM the day before yesterday, confiscating one handgun, seven bullets, and four bombs. They took them back to the police station. According to Gu's confession, the handgun was given to him by his son-in-law, a boatman named Yang, who planned to go to Zhujiajiao, Qingpu, by Yang's boat to commit robberies. The detective went to arrest Yang but could not find him, so he detained the arrested criminals. (2) At 9:15 AM on the 11th of last month, several robbers suddenly broke into the home of Zhang Tangshi at No. 5 Lane 10, Dagu Road, robbing 545 yuan. After reporting to the police, the Xinzha Police Station detectives Ma Zhongrong, Ding Huaguo, Yang Yunfeng, and Patrol Officer Xu Zhengting arrested the robbers Shen Agen, Yang Haiming, and Tao Qiuquan at Room 13, Chunjing Inn, Ningxing Street, French Concession. Subsequently, they arrested Xu Qiukui on Xizang Road and confiscated two handguns, seven bullets, and one fake handgun at Shen Agen's home at No. 14 Xingping Lane, Caishi Road, French Concession. All were taken back to the police station for detention. (3) Gordon Road Police Station Detective Chief Zhu Mengwei and Detective Zhang Liang arrested the robbers Wang Tiechen and Liang Jufang at Maqi Road, Binlang Road, at 6:15 PM on the 4th. They found a handgun and fourteen bullets in Wang's waistband. According to Liang's confession, the gun was given to him by Liu Junchen of No. 733 Liyuan Road, Nanshi. The detective then arrested Liu and temporarily detained him in the Public Security Bureau. Yesterday morning, the police sent all the criminals except Liu Junchen to the Criminal Court No. 8 of the First Special District Court. Police lawyer Qian Xunjiu explained the circumstances of the arrest and requested a postponement for investigation of the crimes committed by the criminals. After questioning by Judge Liu Yugui, he ordered them to be returned to detention for further interrogation at a later date.

Dongjiadu Ferry Accident Continues to be Investigated 114

Boatmen Involved in the Accident Have Been Sent to Court, Number of Drowned Still Awaiting Clarification

The ferries going back and forth between Pudong and Puxi at the various wharves such as the Muddy Beach Wharf, Old White Ferry, etc. in Nanshi used to be operated by manpower. When encountering strong winds and rapid currents, they were extremely dangerous. They have now been gradually converted to ferries or towed by small boats. However, the ferries at the Dongjiadu ferry still employ manual rowing. Every day from 2:00 or 3:00 AM until 1:00 AM in the evening, the number of passengers coming and going is endless. The proceeds are distributed according to shares. Around 6:00 PM the day before yesterday, a ferry boat driven by boatmen Zhao Jintao and Huang Yonghua, carrying more than twenty male and female passengers, was rowing from Puxi to Pudong. When it reached the middle of the river, about five or six zhang away from the Pudong wharf, a Chunhua ship suddenly came from north to south. Because it was sailing at full speed, it was unable to avoid it, and it crashed into the ferry boat amidships, breaking it into two pieces. All the people on the boat fell into the water. Although sixteen people were rescued, five people drowned. (Outside reports say there were as many as eleven people). The water patrol team arrested the boatmen Zhao Jintao and Huang Yonghua who caused the accident and sent them to the Public Security Bureau for questioning. The bodies were being retrieved and other details were reported in the previous news. Now, it is found that the boatmen did not take preventive measures beforehand, resulting in this tragedy. Now they are imprisoned, which is indeed unavoidable. If ferries and small boat towing had been adopted earlier, making navigation faster (it takes only five minutes from Puxi to Pudong), collisions could have been avoided. Yesterday afternoon, the Third Section of the Public Security Bureau questioned Zhao Jintao and Huang Yonghua again and then sent a document dispatching police to transfer them to the District Court for interrogation and legal action. At the same time, it instructed the water patrol team to pay attention to retrieving the bodies and investigate exactly how many people drowned. It instructed the ferry leaders Ji Hegui and Zhao Agou to be responsible for finding out the facts and reporting back for verification.

Baole'an Road, Japanese Thief Attempts to Rob a Tobacco Shop 115

Uses a Cigarette Lighter as a Handgun, Flees After Being Exposed Without a Trace

Yesterday, the Japanese Shanghai Daily reported that at 1:00 AM on the 5th, a Japanese robber broke into the Fuyuan Tobacco Shop, a Chinese-run business at No. 161 Baole'an Road. The shop owner, Lu Cairong, was already in bed. The thief went straight to the second floor, holding something that looked like a handgun, and threatened Lu in Japanese, "Quickly hand over the money!" Lu immediately jumped out of bed. His wife, Mrs. Lu, suddenly turned on the light. Seeing the object held by the thief, she realized it was not a handgun, but a cigarette lighter. The thief, seeing that he had been exposed, quickly tried to escape. Chen immediately gave chase. The thief threw the lighter at Lu and fled. Lu then reported to the Public Works Bureau on Dixiwei Road. The bureau, together with officials from the Japanese Consulate General, rushed to the scene to investigate, but the thief had already escaped. According to Lu's wife, a Japanese Ronin came to Shanghai from Manchuria on the 2nd of this month, lodging on the second floor behind the shop.

Although there were some misunderstandings or matters not permitted by administrative procedures, there were also many points that could be referenced based on academics or proven facts, which should be considered and adopted when revising the regulations to facilitate their implementation. You should be informed, etc., and the implementation was postponed twice. In addition to quietly waiting for the amendments, the associations, for the sake of safeguarding the government's prestige, instructed all members to comply with the regulations in the previous year. Free Talk

On the Use of Colloquialisms 138

— Xing Zhi

Although there is debate in vernacular literature about writing in Mandarin versus local dialects, the insertion of colloquialisms is unavoidable. Therefore, in vernacular literature, the use of colloquialisms does not need to be mentioned.

But strangely, there is also extensive use of colloquialisms in classical literature. From this, we can know that not only is the use of colloquialisms not strange in vernacular literature, but it is also very common in classical Chinese.

The use of colloquialisms is actually a literary element. Using colloquialisms can make literature more vivid. When expression is insufficient, colloquialisms must be used to convey the author's opinions and accurately depict the intended form, regardless of importance or size.

Only shallow craftsmen feel that using colloquialisms damages the elegance of the writing. Therefore, among writers of the past, only masters dared to use colloquialisms, knowing the benefits of doing so. Others were not qualified.

In ancient prose, the Records of the Grand Historian and the Book of Han are renowned. However, the Records of the Grand Historian actually incorporates many colloquialisms, and the Book of Han is praised for its conciseness and luxuriance precisely because it skillfully uses the language of the people at the time. For example, in the Records of the Grand Historian's "Biography of Chen She," there is the line:

"What a guy! Chen She, becoming a king, so majestic!" (The character "者" was pronounced like "睹" in ancient times.)

This sentence perfectly depicts the demeanor of farming friends. "夥頥" is a colloquialism for amazement. Another example is in the "Biography of Zhou Chang," which describes the stuttering Zhou Chang admonishing Emperor Gaozu:

"I cannot speak well, but I know, know that it is not right. Your Majesty wants to depose the heir, I know! I will not obey the decree."

This also vividly imitates the way people speak colloquially.

As for the Book of Han, such as the "Biography of the Empresses," the long memorial of the Sili Jie Guang impeaching the Zhao Feiyan sisters simply uses colloquialisms to record the confessions of palace maids and eunuchs. Therefore, it feels very simple. Because the passage is too long, it is inconvenient to quote it here.

There are also many examples of using colloquialisms in ancient poetry. Du Fu is known as the "Poet Sage," one of the greatest poets in China, but he uses many colloquialisms. For example, in the poem "Sending Cai Xilu":

"The horse's head is close, the brocade on its back is blurred."

"匼匝" (meaning dense) and "模糊" (blurred) are both colloquialisms.

Furthermore, Du Fu often uses the characters "喫" (chi, to eat) and "箇" (ge, a measure word), saying "eat" as "喫" and counting things with "箇." Are these not colloquialisms? For example, "Drinking upstairs, sleeping downstairs," "Just let me eat my fill in my remaining years," "I promised to eat plums with Old Zhu," "Parting is quite sorrowful, I cannot eat when facing wine," and "The mountain stream startles the monkeys hearing '筒' [a bamboo pipe], 'Two 筒s of yellow trick the singing orioles,' 'Instead adding a 筒 to the well curb.'"

As for the poems "Presented to Bi Siyao" and "Early Autumn Suffering from Heat," it can almost be said that the entire poems are written in colloquialisms. Du Fu's greatness can be said to lie in this.

Others such as Ying Qu, Zuo Si, and Cheng Xiao of the Six Dynasties were all vernacular poets who were popular with the people. They especially liked to use colloquialisms. Here is Cheng Xiao's "Mocking a Hot Guest" as an example:

"In my life during the three dog days, there are no carriages on the road. I close the door to avoid the heat and lie down, not visiting each other. Nowadays, 　　children, heat reaches their homes. When the host hears of a guest's arrival, he frowns. Thinking they should leave, they sit and 跘跨, what they say is not urgent, what they like to eat is so much? Tired of it for a long time, only asking "Where are you from?" Shaking his painful thighs, sweat flows down. Do not say it is a small matter, it is also a great flaw. Passing on the precepts, observing brightness, heat traveling should be scolded!"

In this poem, "　　," "跘跨," "嗜啥," and "極那" are all colloquialisms, showing that ancient poets used them often. Others such as "Raise my head and gaze at the bright moon, lower my head and think of my hometown," "Three thousand miles of river water, twelve lines of letters home; each line says nothing else, only that I should return home early," and "A pot of wine beside the bed" are all written entirely in colloquialisms, as clear as plain speech. This shows that colloquialisms do not harm elegance and can help to make the writing lively and fluent.

"Children's Literature" 139

— Gu Ding

This year is Children's Year. The term "children's literature" has also been specifically brought up with the start of the year. To meet this need, the number of children's magazines published by various publishing houses has increased, and there is competition to publish children's libraries and the like. From the perspective of children, this is certainly a good phenomenon.

The majority of children in China have always lived in an atmosphere of "non-culture." A few dry books, some even accompanied by a green bamboo ruler, have nearly all been taught to become "precocious" with lifeless faces. I remember when we were children, we were absolutely forbidden to read literary works or anything similar, whether at home or at school. Some of my friends hid under black quilts, lit a stick of incense, and read "Journey to the West" and the like, almost blinding their eyes. This terrifying past has been forever drowned by the flowing time: surely there should be much more progress now? But I read an article by Mr. Bai Fen on "Taibai" that said "It's hard to teach even smart kids!" It is said that the teacher, in order to make the students feel the class he was teaching, took them to Baoshan Road to take a look, but the next day, the father came to the teacher to reprimand him: "No way!" That's the gist of it. However, it can be imagined that today's children are not necessarily much better than we were then!

However, this year's children can be considered to have had a stroke of good luck. They were always called to hide behind the backs of their fathers and elder brothers, but now they have suddenly been embraced in front of everyone. So, it is inevitable that everyone will point at their small mouths and faces and comment on them, eventually saying: Children should also have literature. Good, I am very willing to raise both hands, because I especially remember the eyes of my little friends from the past. In fact, this question should have been shouted out loudly long ago.

Speaking of "children's literature," according to the Chinese custom of dealing with problems, I am afraid that some people are already scratching their heads and frowning, saying: Half of the year is gone! In fact, the problem is not so simple. It is definitely not something that can be accomplished by some "Ode to Children" to celebrate the occasion. It is serious and arduous work. All those who are truly immersed in culture, truly thinking about the next generation, should have such determination, one year, two years, ten years, a hundred years... to bloom small flowers, and also to bloom big flowers, flourishing and widespread.

To suit the tastes of children, creation is certainly important; but what is especially important for us at present is to cultivate authors. To be practical and rich, we must "learn" from the masterpieces of the world. Translation is even more urgent. Therefore, foreign works should be introduced as much as possible. At the same time, we should be confident that Chinese "children's literature" should be a time of hardship, of cultivation on the one hand, and of creation on the other.

Night Crossing (11) 140

— Zhou Leng

Seeing everyone criticizing her and not one person willing to give her sympathy and tolerance, the young woman couldn't help but shout anxiously.

"By the heavens and earth! I am not an accomplice of robbers! I 　　hid this package on my stomach. Maybe the robbers thought I was fat, so they didn't pay attention."

These words caused everyone in the cabin to burst into laughter. Only Mr. Xunqing did not laugh. He kept stroking his beard, sometimes incidentally reaching up to stroke his right cheek.

After laughing for a while, Grandma Degui coldly began to speak again.

"Hmph! No one, not even a three-year-old child, would be fooled by such words. Robbers have such sharp eyes. The gold hairpin on my head, almost half of it buried in my hair, was searched away by them. How could they have missed such a large package?"

Mr. Xunqing raised one hand high, striking a pose like an old magistrate passing judgment.

"Alright, this is enough to prove that she is an accomplice of robbers. Another suspicious thing is that her face is very unfamiliar. I have lived here for so many years and don't seem to have seen her before. Is there anyone among you who recognizes her?"

Eight or nine out of ten people in the cabin shook their heads. The only ones who didn't shake their heads were Liu Cangshui, Dongsheng, and Abao. They also didn't recognize the young woman, but they were somewhat dissatisfied with Mr. Xunqing's arrogant attitude. However, they all understood that their status was very low and they were definitely no match for Mr. Xunqing, who was known as the "Red Serpent." Therefore, although they felt sorry for the young woman, they dared not say anything.

The young woman seemed to be suffocating from the cabin's cold atmosphere and began to sob softly. Suddenly, she stood up resolutely and said to the crowd, choking with sobs:

"Everyone here is sensible. If I were an accomplice of robbers, why wouldn't I have left with the robbers? This gentleman is clearly trying to frame me. I don't know who he is, but just now in the dark, he reached out to touch... touch me..."

"Touched what?" Wu Hexuan asked slyly, full of interest, while glaring fiercely at Mr. Xunqing.

"Touched my breasts!" The young woman continued, her face reddening. "I shouldn't have slapped him. I didn't expect him to hold a grudge and now bite me back, insisting that I'm an accomplice of robbers!"

"Hmph, hmph!" Wu Hexuan couldn't help but sneer at Mr. Xunqing twice in a row. He secretly felt delighted, thinking that Mr. Xunqing's hypocritical mask was now completely torn off. The eyes of the people in the cabin were also stunned and fixed on Mr. Xunqing's face, as if they were all surprised that such a stern and rigid person would also do shady things in secret.

Courtesy 141

— Xu Ying

As usual, in the evening, I locked the door of the small school and took the key home for dinner. My home was a single room in Zhongyu's small family. Thanks to his wife and him, this lone person could eat with them.

Being immersed in dealing with a jumble of things all day, I only found tranquility at this time. I was happiest leaning on that bamboo back chair, listening to my own heartbeat and listening to the young couple's laughter.

Today was especially early. I specially went back to tell them, fearing that the woman would be anxious, since Zhongyu had accompanied the bank's inspector into the city and might not return for a day. When I left, there was still half of the setting sun remaining in the sky.

When I got home, the brown thatched roof made people feel warm at first glance. As I entered, the old yellow dog wagged its tail in its sleep to welcome me. The courtyard set off by the courtyard house was square and tidy. A row of large sunflowers with big heads was placed there, their colors harmonizing perfectly with the white walls.

Listening, it seemed that someone was talking in the main room. I was inconvenienced to go in and disturb them, so I swallowed the words that were on my lips and went straight to my room. The room was shady and very cool.

I sat on the bamboo chair with a backrest and whistled. I thanked my little landlord. She had already prepared a large bottle of cold boiled water for me. I raised the bottle and poured it down my throat in one breath.

I whistled again: I closed my eyes…

"Mr. Li, when did you come back?..."

It was dark. Zhongyu's wife came in to deliver a kerosene lamp. She shouted loudly, and I woke up from my drowsiness.

"What happened?" I said, laughing. "I fell asleep as soon as I sat down..."

I stood up and told her that Zhongyu had gone into the city. She listened indifferently. A minute later, she spat and looked straight at me with her big, round eyes, saying, "Wait a moment, I have something to ask of you..."

The woman in the blue robe went out, her black hair bouncing on her head.

A smile floated on my face. In a moment, I saw the woman come in carrying a bamboo basket of pink eggs, her expression very solemn.

"Giving gifts?" I couldn't help but joke. "Seems a bit early for the old nephew—isn't it?"

She glared at me fiercely, and a rose-red color flew onto her cheeks. She lowered her head, her hand pressing on her bulging abdomen. Since she became pregnant, she had refused to go out and dared not see strangers. She was teaching a class in the small school, and at this time she had to give it to her husband. Only I, their only neighbor, often made fun of her about this.

"I'm talking about serious matters," she said, feigning anger. "This was sent to you by an old relative of mine. She said that you have already investigated the fields for the loan, and she wants to ask you to add 20,000 or 30,000 to the loan and temporarily calculate it as first class..."

"This!" I put away my smile. "This is not easy to do."

I thought that it would be difficult to handle loans of more than 20,000 without "fairness." Although bribery was rampant, it was definitely not allowed to exist in the fledgling cooperative. Although, because of emotion, I could not explain it to her in white (in fact, she also understood), so I could only say:

"Please return this gift to her and ask her to write down her name. I can check if there is any false reporting..."

When Zhongyu's wife heard my "official talk," she believed that she was avoiding misunderstandings and insistence on the matter. I had to change the atmosphere and start laughing again: "But, I will eat your red eggs."

After a pleasant supper, I went to the adult night school to teach.

Old Maid 142

— Sheng Shi

Every year in spring,

Leaves behind a sigh.

In unspeakable resentment,

She watches the tender green of youth pass away.

Her cheeks turn a dull, waxy yellow,

No longer able to conjure a smile on her lips.

Those full, beautiful curves,

Have lost their lightness.

Submerged in boundless loneliness,

A resentful heart.

Old Sheep 143

— Shen Shengshi

His surname was Liang. His meek and kind temperament was like a sheep's. Our companions all called him—Old Sheep.

Old Sheep was one of the most pitiful among our companions.

Timid, with sensitive, nervous qualities, his blood always flowed with the germs of sadness and loneliness.

He was always telling us wild tales, having strange dreams in the daytime, always holding onto negativity. He told us many times, always saying:

—A person can't live like this any longer. Every hour I ask myself, what reason do I have to live? On moonlit nights, I ask the moon, silently gazing at the wobbly stars. I think my own life is hanging in mid-air with no support.

We often comforted him with sympathy, but Old Sheep couldn't be persuaded. In helpless situations, we sighed for him:

—Old Sheep's illness will not get better!

A few years ago, his lung disease was in its second stage, and he still didn't know how to take care of himself. A fellow villager of his told us: When Old Sheep's lung disease was severe, he vomited a lot of blood every day. Because he was the only son in his family, and his father died when he was young, his mother's last hope was on him. However, during Old Sheep's serious lung disease, he still planned to kill himself every day. His mother, watching his large piles of blood, hugged his thin, out-of-shape body, and cried:

—My son! Don't vomit, okay? Don't vomit anymore!

A bag of tears in her old eyes, aching, fell out.

His mother spent thousands of medical expenses to treat him, and his lung disease finally slowly improved after a long period of recuperation.

In his 19th year, Old Sheep was married by his family.

He was not satisfied with this clumsy new wife who had lived in the countryside since childhood.

It wasn't until he became our close classmate at × Middle School that he told us:

—I couldn't bear to go against my mother's wish for me to get married, but on the day of the wedding, I planned to escape. Later, my secret was seen through by my family and I couldn't escape. On the seventh day after the wedding, I decided to say goodbye to my mother and go to the city to study.

—Let me tell you, I have never acknowledged this woman. I didn't talk to her for seven days and seven nights. She's clumsy and stupid, doesn't know a single character, and has an ugly appearance. I can't explain to myself why I should love such an annoying woman.

Every time he talked about his own problem, his heart would be broken, and some unresolvable sadness would all attack him together.

We explained to him that there was nothing in the world that couldn't be solved. Couples who couldn't be together could divorce. We knew that he must have thought about it too, but he felt that there were various difficulties for the other party, so he gave up.

He looked at life with depressed eyes, but he was a young man full of emotion, often letting his overly sensitive nerves run wild, thinking about the vague, unrestrained sky. He had no grasp on life, and only cursed this chaotic society. He felt that life had no hope, no foundation, in a world where he couldn't find a way out. He was dejected and depressed.

Old Sheep's illness would not get better. He was a bottle of sake that had run out of air.

When a person reaches a state of extreme sadness, their mind becomes sick. We knew that he had a female classmate at school whom he wanted to love but dared not, but he cursed them for being vain every day, gnashing his teeth and cursing that women's hearts were the most poisonous. He told us that he wanted to go to a desolate mountain temple to become a monk.

Every evening, when we talked to him, his emotions would become uncontrollably excited. While talking to us, he would suddenly shout out, and a layer of sweat would ooze from his forehead. A face that was usually brownish-yellow would turn red, sadly smiling sourly, and crying in the end.

I didn't dare to talk to him casually. I couldn't bear to hear a companion's laughter that turned into crying.

It had been almost three years since we parted ways. Although I had met him once in between, his temperament didn't seem to have changed. I thought Old Sheep's illness would not easily get better.

Tonight, the wind is howling. I am also gazing at the wobbly stars in the sky. Under the full sky of stars, does he also know that a lonely heart is remembering him?

Educational News

Local Elementary School Teachers Celebrate Teachers' Day Yesterday 144

Over 500 Faculty and Staff Attended; Bureau Chief Pan and Section Chief Chen Gave Speeches

Yesterday was Teachers' Day. All the combatant teachers of municipal elementary schools held a celebration meeting at the auditorium of Wuben Girls' Middle School at 10 a.m. yesterday. More than 500 teachers from various schools attended. Details are recorded as follows:

Celebration Details The celebration meeting began at 10 a.m. The presidium included Xu Shushen, Qian Xuanqing, and Hu Huaitian. After performing the rituals, Chairman Xu Shushen first reported on the significance of Teachers' Day, followed by a speech by Yu Zhongbiao, the representative of the Municipal Party Department. Bureau Chief Pan and Section Chief Chen of the Municipal Education Bureau then gave speeches. Afterward, a group photo was taken, and the meeting adjourned. At noon, a luncheon was held at the Tongxinglou restaurant on Fourth Avenue. In the afternoon, participants traveled by car to Yeyuan in Jiangwan for sightseeing.

Speech by Mr. Pan Bureau Chief Pan's speech briefly stated: "Today, municipal elementary school teachers are celebrating Teachers' Day here. I am very happy to attend and express my gratitude on behalf of the elementary school students. The chairman mentioned earlier that while teachers' material life may be relatively simple, they find great comfort in their spiritual lives. When we celebrate Teachers' Day, the value of the celebration should be directly proportional to the achievements of the students we teach, rather than the amount of material goods. If we hope to make the celebration meaningful, we must work hard in teaching students. Elementary school students are more numerous than middle and high school students, and all middle and high school students have passed through the elementary school stage. Therefore, all students have been taught by you. Your responsibilities are significant, and you receive much spiritual comfort. Today, taking the opportunity of Teachers' Day, I would like to talk to you about a famous teacher. Confucius is a pioneer teacher, a predecessor of teachers, and already famous both domestically and internationally. However, his achievements were entirely in education. He taught three thousand disciples. Teaching so many students in the Spring and Autumn period was not easy. Confucius said, 'Learning without satiety, teaching without weariness.' These two sentences are the standards that teachers should adhere to throughout their lives. Teachers should not be weary. If they constantly dislike life in their hearts, they will be weary. This will affect their work, so they must have the spirit of courage and diligence to teach without weariness. However, while teaching without weariness is important, learning without satiety is also important. If we only use what we have learned in the past to teach, we will definitely run out of knowledge. Especially now, everything is progressing at every moment. We must keep up with the times. Confucius said, 'Reviewing the old and knowing the new.' This is the annotation of learning without satiety. If you can do both, you are a complete teacher. I hope you will work hard to achieve this, and your harvest will increase with time."

Hong Kong Education Sector (Hong Kong, 6th) June 6th is Teachers' Day. The Hong Kong education sector held a celebration meeting at the Entertainment Theatre at 9 a.m. Two thousand faculty and staff from various schools participated.

Guangdong Education Association (Central News Agency, Hong Kong, 6th) The Guangzhou Municipal Primary Education Association held a meeting at the Minjiao Hall at 1 p.m. on the 8th to celebrate Teachers' Day. A general membership meeting was held on the 7th to discuss improving teachers' lives and important education matters.

Hangzhou Middle and High Schools (Hangzhou, 6th) At 8 a.m. this morning, approximately 2,000 teachers from large, middle, and small schools in Hangzhou celebrated Teachers' Day at the Lianhua Cinema. Zheng Zixiang presided over the meeting. Representatives from the Party Department, Municipal Government, and Education Bureau gave speeches, and the film "Spring River Flower Moon Night" was screened. The meeting adjourned at 11 a.m.

Comparison of Teachers' Teaching and Remuneration in Elementary Schools in Various Countries 147

The Ministry of Education has compiled statistics on the remuneration of elementary school teachers in various countries, as well as the gender ratio and the average number of students per teacher. A summary is provided below:

(1) Teacher Remuneration The remuneration of elementary school teachers in various countries is first converted to pounds sterling and then to Chinese currency. The annual salary of teachers in: Republic of China: 24 to 1800 yuan (the highest is 1800 yuan per year for Hubei teachers, and the lowest is 24 yuan per year for Shaanxi teachers); United Kingdom: 2303 to 5594 yuan; United States: 3948 to 7897 yuan; Italy: 836 to 412 yuan; France: 987 to 1769 yuan; Germany: 1878 to 3359 yuan; Soviet Russia: 946 to 1069 yuan; Japan: 343 to 4044 yuan; Canada: 1865 to 4648 yuan; Australia: 4264 to 5470 yuan; Netherlands: 1138 to 3510 yuan; Belgium: 1015 to 2029 yuan; Sweden: 3016 yuan; Denmark: 1673 to 3661 yuan; Austria: 658 to 2152 yuan; Hungary: 740 to 1535 yuan; Switzerland: 1631 to 3044 yuan; Norway: 2646 to 6046 yuan; South Africa: 1851 to 5553 yuan; Poland: 480 yuan. (Note: In China, the United States, Italy, France, Germany, Russia, the Netherlands, Belgium, Austria, Hungary, and Poland, the remuneration for male and female elementary school teachers is the same. In all other countries, female teachers are paid less than male teachers.)

(2) Teacher Teaching The average number of students per elementary school teacher in various countries: China: 19.9 students per teacher in public elementary schools and 28.3 students per teacher in private elementary schools. (The following abbreviations are used for public and private schools, and decimal points are omitted.) United Kingdom: 33 public; France: 27 public, 25 private; Germany: 36 public, 25 private; Italy: 44 public; Soviet Russia: 41 public; Canada: 32 public; Australia: 37 public, 24 private; Spain: 51 public, 35 private; Belgium: 26 public; Netherlands: 32 public; Greece: 52 public, 28 private; Hungary: 49 public; Sweden: 34 public; Switzerland: 28 public; Turkey: 46 public, 46 private; Denmark: 32 public, 16 private; Portugal: 37 public; Austria: 34 public, 24 private; Poland: 50 public, 22 private; Finland: 31 public, 17 private; Romania: 45 public.

(3) Teacher Gender The percentage of male and female elementary school teachers in various countries: China: 97% male, 3% female; Australia: 40% male, 60% female; Austria: 57% male, 43% female; Belgium: 43% male, 57% female; Canada: 19% male, 81% female; Czechoslovakia: 74% male, 116% female; Denmark: 64% male, 36% female; United Kingdom: 24% male, 76% female; Finland: 30% male, 70% female; France: 35% male, 65% female; Germany: 75% male, 25% female; Netherlands: 56% male, 44% female; Hungary: 57% male, 43% female; Ireland: 35% male, 65% female; Japan: 67% male, 33% female; New Zealand: 36% male, 64% female; Norway: 65% male, 35% female; Poland: 43% male, 57% female; Scotland: 21% male, 79% female; Soviet Russia: 29% male, 71% female; South Africa: 40% male, 60% female; Sweden: 29% male, 71% female; Switzerland: 50% male, 50% female; United States: 11% male, 89% female.

The Municipal Council Decides on Selection Method

The American Boy Scout 25th Anniversary Meeting will be held in mid-August this year. The China Boy Scout General Association has decided to send Boy Scout representatives and has designated three representatives from each of Jiangsu, Zhejiang, Hebei, Hubei, Shanghai, Beijing, and Ping provinces and cities to go to Beijing for the examination. The Shanghai Municipal Boy Scout Council has instructed various groups to prepare yesterday and has scheduled each Boy Scout group to send one Boy Scout to the Minli Girls' Middle School on Wenmiao Road in the city on June 9 to participate in the preliminary examination. The Council's selection methods are copied below.

Selection Method

(1) Organize a selection committee for the city's representatives to the American Boy Scout meeting. The council will appoint one person each from the Minjiao Museum and the Health Bureau, as well as Yu Zhongyi, Gu Shunhua, Leng Xueqiao, Qu Yue, Luo Lie, Gong Jingyuan, Jin Xing, Zhang Xunfang, and other committee members. (2) The preliminary examination will be held at the Minli Girls' Middle School at 1 p.m. on June 9. All registered and approved school and social Boy Scout groups in the city may send one Boy Scout each to participate in the examination. In addition to all the examination committee members attending to conduct the examination, the executive director will serve as the chief examiner, and all directors will supervise the examination. (3) Selection standards: (1) Age: 14 to 18 years old; (2) Qualifications: Passed the intermediate course examination and completed five or more advanced courses, and certified by the group leader; (3) Physical condition: Height of 5 feet, healthy physique, good posture, and internal organs examined by a doctor and certified as qualified; (4) Examination items: (1) Intermediate course: etiquette, hygiene, Morse code, semaphore, English semaphore, orientation, military step, reconnaissance, fire starting, first aid, cooking; (2) Advanced course: English Morse code, surveying, cartography, swimming, travel knowledge (including camping knowledge); (3) Special courses: bicycle, sports, bugle, photography, translation (limited to Chinese and English); (4) Special skills: Jianzi kicking, Tai Chi, martial arts, performance, English conversation; (5) Oral examination: Civic knowledge, Boy Scout knowledge; (5) Passing standards: In addition to the physical examination by the Health Bureau doctor, which must be qualified, all courses and oral examinations will be examined according to the training standards set by the General Association. Special skills will be selected by experts. The top three performers in the overall score will be selected as the city's representatives; (6) The evaluation form for each subject will be determined separately.

Sports News

Renowned Chinese and Western Handball Players to Perform in Beijing Today 157

Participating in the Inauguration Ceremony of the Lizi Society Handball Court; The Youth Association Specially Compiles a Handball Book to Commemorate

Two newly built handball courts at the Lizi Society in Nanjing will hold their inauguration ceremony tomorrow. Huang Renlin, the secretary-general of the Society, and Qian Yiqin, the sports officer, have come to Shanghai to consult with Ling Xitao, the sports officer of the Shanghai Youth Association, to invite renowned Chinese and Western handball players to participate in the inauguration ceremony in Beijing. The situation of all parties is recorded below:

The Most Complete in the Far East The Lizi Society in Nanjing has always been known for its perfect sports facilities. Recognizing the benefits of handball for health, it has newly built two handball courts in the Society, 20 feet wide and 40 feet long, with walls on three sides and a glass roof. It is the most complete handball court in the Far East, in order to actively promote handball. The invitation of renowned Chinese and Western players to perform this time has aroused the interest of people there and is a precursor to future handball matches between Beijing and Shanghai.

A Brief History of Chinese and Western Players Those invited to Beijing this time, Zhu Kuan, Sun Daosheng, Hong Yukui, Hua Fenggang, Clyde Meyer, and Ling Xitao of the Chinese Youth Association, will travel to Beijing by car today and will take turns performing doubles and singles matches in Beijing tomorrow and the day after. A brief introduction of each person is as follows: (1) Zhu Kuan, peerless, unparalleled, and has unique skills in hitting the board. Shanghai's renowned Chinese and Western players have all conceded defeat. He has won the Shanghai Open Handball Singles Championship twice. His fame is as great as Li Huitang in the football world. (2) Sun Daosheng has practiced handball for more than ten years and has made great contributions to the development of handball. He is quite old and physically weak, relying on his skills to surpass others. Almost everyone in the Chinese and Western handball community knows this veteran. (3) Hong Yukui, a young hero, is full of muscle, has superb skills, and is rich in experience. He can cooperate with Zhu Kuan to participate in the Shanghai Open Doubles Handball Competition, winning the championship in the first edition and the runner-up in the second edition. (4) Hua Fenggang, an outstanding talent among the new players, has made rapid progress in skills in the past year, attracting everyone's attention. He is brave and resilient and is the best among his peers. He uses his left and right arms freely, and he never misses a returning ball. (5) Clyde Meyer has won the Western Youth Handball Grade Championship and the runner-up in the Second Shanghai Open Singles. He is physically great but extremely skillful. His right hand is especially good. He can take care of the left side and can use one hand for one purpose. He has excellent combat spirit and superior strategy. He is the mainstay of the Western team.

Congratulatory Letter from Director Pan Pan Gongzhan, Director of the Shanghai Municipal Education Bureau, sent a dozen handballs to congratulate the Society on the completion of the handball court and personally sent a letter to Huang Renlin, the Secretary-General of the Society. Now, the comrades in the Chinese and Western handball community here will jointly go to Beijing to participate in the opening ceremony of your Society's handball court. I have specially entrusted them to bring twelve handballs to mark the occasion. Please accept them. I hope and pray for it. (Omitted below)

Commemorative Compilation of Handball The Shanghai International Handball Competition, the 5th and 6th editions of the Gongzhan Cup, are owned by the Chinese team. Successful Production of Chinese-Made Baseballs 163

New product from Xie Xing Sporting Goods Factory

The Xie Xing Sporting Goods Factory on Weier Meng Road in this city is a large-scale Chinese manufacturer of sporting goods. It was founded in 1914 by Mr. Zhang Zhongwen, who has painstakingly managed it for over 20 years. They produce everything from soccer balls, basketballs, volleyballs, rugby balls, related accessories, track and field equipment, tennis rackets, swimming suits, running shoes, etc., all of which are exquisitely made. Recently, they have created baseballs that are comparable to foreign goods, earning high praise from the Chinese people. They have also successfully manufactured gloves, batting helmets, and other equipment used in baseball games. With the assistance of his younger brother, Zhongying, Mr. Zhang's products are even better, and his business is thriving.

Finance: One Day Trend, From Low to High; Premium Rises Again by Eight Dollars 167

Rumors That Hong Kong Is Cooperating with China to Ban Silver Outflow; Even With Large-Scale Selling by Major Players, the Final Trend Remains Very Strong

The gold market yesterday, amid the closure period, saw foreign silver fall and rise. Immediately upon opening, it rose, but weakened slightly midway due to large-scale selling by major players. Foreign news reported that the Hong Kong government is cooperating with our country to ban silver outflow, leading to a surprisingly strong close. In the early morning, due to the approaching closure period, foreign telegrams reported that British and American silver markets had fallen. "Big feet" [market players] claimed that the market weakened after closing due to selling by Chinese speculators and that the final transaction was 25 lower. The forward silver price in Montevideo also fell by 1.9%. Exchange rates generally rose. London pure gold fell by 9.5 pence. News reports varied, and although sentiment was strong, it appeared somewhat uncertain. Outside the market, pre-market trading opened at 756 yuan. Unexpectedly, many who entered late faced high prices, and the market gradually declined. The Central Bank's official rates were released, reflecting reduced British and American rates. Customs gold units rose by 1.2%. The standard premium price was listed at 837 yuan and 7 jiao, with only a slight rally in the middle. The morning opening was quite flat. After opening, major players entered aggressively at low prices, immediately pulling the market up. The Jewish merchant Qiao Zhifu sold shillings, and the HSBC rates were released, with British rates flat and American rates up by 0.25. Soon after, the market trended downwards, but banks showed considerable appetite, supporting the market. When the Chinese Merchants Bank also came to support, the exchange rate tightened, and the market rose by 0.07. However, due to outflows from domestic goods and Guangdong merchants, many took profits at the high, and the decline was rapid. However, the 70-yuan mark was not broken. Banks took advantage of the momentum to continue supporting, and sentiment remained stable. Subsequently, the market was stable for quite some time. Finally, sentiment shifted from extreme calm to a desire for movement, and buying interest increased, resulting in a strong recovery in the afternoon. In the post-market, the news of small Indian silver sparked buying interest and a rise, but major players continued to sell, causing a renewed decline. Reuters reported that the Hong Kong market softened due to falling Indian silver and news that the United States would change its silver purchasing policy. Although there was a rise, at this time, Indian silver rebounded by 0.06, but soon stabilized. Guangdong merchants made some purchases. A Reuters report citing Hong Kong financial circles stated that the Hong Kong government's ban on silver exports sparked buying interest and pushed the market close to the 80-yuan mark. Many continued to sell, and the upward trend was temporarily halted, but the final close was still strong. After the close, Associated Press reported that the Hong Kong government was meeting to cooperate with China to ban silver outflow, causing a further rise. This was due to the tightening of exchange rates, and both Hong Kong and Shanghai were expected to face a shortage of funds.
